[2024-02-20 14:43:02.917976] DEBUG: runsink: Why is the sky blue?
[2024-02-20 14:43:26.800144] DEBUG: runsink: The sky appears blue to the human eye because of the scattering of sunlight by the Earth's atmosphere. Sunlight is made up of different colors of light that have various wavelengths. When sunlight enters the Earth's atmosphere, it collides with molecules and particles in the atmosphere. 

Blue light has shorter wavelengths and more energy compared to other colors. Because of its short wavelength, blue light is scattered in all directions by the tiny molecules of air in the Earth's atmosphere much more efficiently than other colors. This scattering causes the direct sunlight that looks white to our eyes to take on a blue hue in the sky. 

This phenomenon is known as Rayleigh scattering, named after the British physicist Lord Rayleigh who first described it in the 19th century. The effect of Rayleigh scattering is also why sunsets and sunrises often appear red or orange. At sunrise and sunset, the light has to travel through more of the Earth's atmosphere to reach your eyes. This longer path through the atmosphere allows more blue light to be scattered out of the direct line of sight, leaving the longer wavelengths of red and orange to dominate the observed spectrum of sunlight.
[2024-02-20 15:04:34.683904] DEBUG: runsink: Why is water wet?
[2024-02-20 15:04:59.436628] DEBUG: runsink: Water is often described as "wet" because of how it interacts with different materials, including our skin, and the sensations and effects it induces. This experience of water as "wet" can be attributed to a combination of factors:

1. **Cohesion and Adhesion:** Water molecules exhibit strong cohesive forces, meaning they tend to stick to each other due to hydrogen bonding. They also have adhesive properties, meaning they can adhere to many other types of substances. When water comes into contact with a surface, these properties allow it to spread out and form a thin film, which can make the surface feel "wet."

2. **Sensation on Skin:** The interaction between water molecules and human skin results in a distinct sensation. Water can reduce the friction between skin and other surfaces (like when we wash our hands), and this change in how things feel contributes to our perception of wetness.

3. **Temperature Change:** When water evaporates from a surface, including our skin, it absorbs heat, which can lead to a cooling sensation. This evaporation-induced cooling further enhances our perception of wetness.

It's important to note that "wetness" is not an inherent property of water itself, but rather a description of our subjective experience and the outcomes of water's interactions with other materials. The term "wet" is used to describe the state or sensation that results when a liquid comes into contact with a solid, often leading to the liquid spreading over the surface of the solid.

[2024-02-23 17:10:52.283424] DEBUG: runsink: why is the sky blue?
[2024-02-23 17:10:57.753124] DEBUG: runsink: The sky appears blue to the human eye because of the way Earth's atmosphere scatters sunlight. Sunlight is made up of different colors of light, which are scattered in all directions by the gases and particles in the Earth's atmosphere. Blue light is scattered more than other colors because it travels as shorter, smaller waves. This phenomenon is known as Rayleigh scattering. When we look towards the sky away from the sun, we see the scattered blue light more than other colors, making the sky appear blue.
[2024-02-23 17:12:59.925500] DEBUG: runsink: why is water wet?
[2024-02-23 17:13:12.728342] DEBUG: runsink: Water is perceived as "wet" due to the way its molecules interact with the molecules of other substances, including those that make up our skin. Here’s a more detailed explanation:

1. **Cohesion:** Water molecules are attracted to each other due to hydrogen bonding. This strong attraction between water molecules creates a cohesive force that allows water to form droplets and flow smoothly.

2. **Adhesion:** Water molecules also have the capability to adhere or stick to the molecules of other materials. When water comes into contact with a surface, the adhesive forces enable the water molecules to spread out and wet the surface.

3. **Surface Tension:** The cohesive forces at the surface of water create a sort of "skin" or surface tension, making it capable of supporting very light objects and forming droplets that can move across surfaces.

When you touch water, the sensation of wetness is actually a complex interaction involving the thermal and tactile receptors in your skin. The water causes a change in the thermal properties at the surface of your skin and also changes the tactile sensations by reducing friction. These changes in sensory inputs are interpreted by your brain as the sensation of wetness.

In essence, "wetness" is not a property of water itself but rather an experience or sensation created by the interaction of water with our nervous system.

[2024-02-24 15:09:15.603680] DEBUG: runsink: Why is the sky blue?
[2024-02-24 15:09:20.638429] DEBUG: runsink: The sky appears blue to the human eye because of the way Earth's atmosphere scatters sunlight. Sunlight is made up of different colors of light, which are blended together to form what we perceive as white light. When sunlight enters the Earth's atmosphere, it collides with molecules in the air, primarily nitrogen and oxygen.

This scattering process, known as Rayleigh scattering, is more effective at shorter wavelengths. Blue light has a shorter wavelength than other colors within the visible spectrum. Therefore, when sunlight passes through the atmosphere, the blue wavelengths are scattered more widely than others, making the sky look blue under normal daylight conditions.

[2024-03-01 18:37:52.341281] DEBUG: runsink: Eyes appear blue due to a lack of pigment in the iris. The blue coloration is actually not a result of blue pigment but rather a result of the way light is scattered in the stroma, the fibrous tissue in the iris. 

This phenomenon is similar to Rayleigh scattering, which also causes the sky to appear blue. In people with blue eyes, the stroma contains less melanin, the pigment that normally provides eyes with their brown coloration. When light enters the eye with a low concentration of melanin, shorter blue wavelengths of light are scattered back out, while other wavelengths are absorbed or reflected less. This scattered light combines to give the eye its blue appearance. 

The genetics behind eye color are complex, involving multiple genes that influence the level of melanin in the iris.

[2024-03-01 20:42:12.895390] DEBUG: runsink: The color of human eyes is determined by the amount and distribution of melanin in the iris, the colored part of the eye. Blue eyes have the least amount of melanin in the iris. When light enters the eye, it is scattered and reflected by the iris. In eyes with little melanin, such as blue eyes, light undergoes a scattering process known as Rayleigh scattering, which is the same physical principle that causes the sky to appear blue. This scattering process results in the blue coloration observed in the eyes. Essentially, the color is not due to blue pigment but rather the way light interacts with the eye's structure and the low melanin concentration.

[2024-03-03 15:05:09.681416] DEBUG: runsink: The sky appears blue to human observers due to a phenomenon called Rayleigh scattering. This scattering occurs when sunlight enters the Earth's atmosphere and interacts with the particles and molecules in the air. Sunlight, or white light, is made up of different colors of light that have different wavelengths. Blue light has shorter wavelengths and is scattered in all directions more than other colors because it travels as shorter, smaller waves. This means when we look at the sky away from the sun, we see more blue than other colors. As the sun moves lower in the sky, the light must pass through more atmosphere, causing more scattering of the blue light, allowing reds and oranges to become more dominant, which is why sunsets can appear red and orange.

[2024-03-15 17:12:16.544221] DEBUG: runsink: why are eyes blue?
[2024-03-15 17:12:29.920732] DEBUG: runsink: The color of human eyes, including blue eyes, is determined by the pigmentation of the eye's iris and the scattering of light by it. The main factors contributing to eye color are:

1. **Pigmentation**: The iris of the eye contains a pigment called melanin, which is also what determines skin and hair color. The amount and type of melanin in the iris can affect the color of the eyes. People with a lot of melanin in their irises have brown eyes, while those with a little melanin have lighter-colored eyes, such as blue or green.

2. **Light Scattering**: The Tyndall effect, a form of Rayleigh scattering, is another reason for blue eyes. This is a physical process where small particles suspended in a transparent medium scatter light. In the case of the iris with low melanin, the longer wavelengths of light pass through, and the shorter wavelengths (the blues) are scattered, giving the iris a blue appearance.

It is important to note that All humans have the potential for blue eyes. This is because the basics of the eye color are determined genetically, and changes in the genes responsible for melanin production and distribution in the iris lead to variations in eye color among individuals. Specifically, changes in the OCA2 gene and other genes can reduce the amount of melanin produced, leading to lighter eye colors like blue.
